# Skyrim:Skills

## Overview

The skills menu

There are 18 **skills** in [Skyrim](/wiki/Skyrim:Skyrim "Skyrim:Skyrim"), each of which determines how well various tasks can be performed. As skills are used, they increase in level, which increases the character's overall level. The starting value for most skills is 15, although each [race](/wiki/Skyrim:Races "Skyrim:Races") confers bonuses to certain skills. Skills can also be increased by reading [skill books](/wiki/Skyrim:Skill_Books "Skyrim:Skill Books"), learning from [trainers](/wiki/Skyrim:Trainers "Skyrim:Trainers"), or [as a reward](/wiki/Skyrim:Free_Skill_Boosts "Skyrim:Free Skill Boosts") for completing certain quests.

Guards will often [comment](/wiki/Skyrim:Guard_Dialogue#Reactions_to_Player.27s_Skill_Level "Skyrim:Guard Dialogue") on your skills when you are near them.

| Total Perks (180/251) † | | |
| --- | --- | --- |
| [Magic](/wiki/Skyrim:Magic_Overview "Skyrim:Magic Overview") (73/86) | [Combat](/wiki/Skyrim:Combat "Skyrim:Combat") (55/91) | [Stealth](/wiki/Skyrim:Stealth "Skyrim:Stealth") (52/74) |
| [Alteration](/wiki/Skyrim:Alteration "Skyrim:Alteration") (10/14) | [Archery](/wiki/Skyrim:Archery "Skyrim:Archery") (9/16) | [Alchemy](/wiki/Skyrim:Alchemy "Skyrim:Alchemy") (9/15) |
| [Conjuration](/wiki/Skyrim:Conjuration "Skyrim:Conjuration") (15/16) | [Block](/wiki/Skyrim:Block "Skyrim:Block") (9/13) | [Light Armor](/wiki/Skyrim:Light_Armor "Skyrim:Light Armor") (6/10) |
| [Destruction](/wiki/Skyrim:Destruction "Skyrim:Destruction") (14/17) | [Heavy Armor](/wiki/Skyrim:Heavy_Armor "Skyrim:Heavy Armor") (8/12) | [Lockpicking](/wiki/Skyrim:Lockpicking "Skyrim:Lockpicking") (11/11) |
| [Enchanting](/wiki/Skyrim:Enchanting "Skyrim:Enchanting") (9/13) | [One-handed](/wiki/Skyrim:One-handed "Skyrim:One-handed") (10/21) | [Pickpocket](/wiki/Skyrim:Pickpocket "Skyrim:Pickpocket") (8/12) |
| [Illusion](/wiki/Skyrim:Illusion "Skyrim:Illusion") (13/13) | [Smithing](/wiki/Skyrim:Smithing "Skyrim:Smithing") (10/10) | [Sneak](/wiki/Skyrim:Sneak "Skyrim:Sneak") (9/13) |
| [Restoration](/wiki/Skyrim:Restoration "Skyrim:Restoration") (12/13) | [Two-handed](/wiki/Skyrim:Two-handed "Skyrim:Two-handed") (9/19) | [Speech](/wiki/Skyrim:Speech "Skyrim:Speech") (9/13) |

**† (Unique Perks/All Ranks)**

## Perks

Perks are a new feature in Skyrim. Each skill has its own associated perks, which can be unlocked when a character advances a [level](/wiki/Skyrim:Leveling "Skyrim:Leveling"). 180 skill perks are available, 251 if including all ranks for each perk. The perks are all detailed on the individual skill pages, along with their requirements. One perk point is given to the character when the character's overall level increases. The maximum value for unused perk points is 255, four more than required for every perk. Leveling up with 255 unused perk points will cause the counter to roll back to zero and restart.

Most perks have both a skill level requirement and a prerequisite perk that must first be unlocked to make the perk available.

- When a prerequisite perk has more than one rank, only the first rank needs to be unlocked to make the next perk available. For example, to unlock [Enchanting](/wiki/Skyrim:Enchanting "Skyrim:Enchanting")'s "Fire Enchanter" skill, only the first rank of "Enchanter" needs to be unlocked, *not* all five ranks.
- When a skill has two prerequisite perks, only one of the two perks needs to be unlocked to make the next perk available. For example, to unlock the "Extra Effect" skill under Enchanting, only "Storm Enchanter" or "Corpus Enchanter" needs to be unlocked.
- Perk points cannot be changed or undone once spent.
  - With [Dragonborn](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn") installed, perks may be undone and redistributed at the cost of one [dragon](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon "Skyrim:Dragon") soul per skill tree once you have completed the add-on's main quest. See [this page](/wiki/Skyrim:At_the_Summit_of_Apocrypha#Notes "Skyrim:At the Summit of Apocrypha") for details.
  - The [Official Skyrim Patch version 1.9](/wiki/Skyrim:Patch#Patch_1.9 "Skyrim:Patch") allows a skill at level 100 to be made Legendary, which will reset the skill to level 15 and refund all perk points allocated to that skill, making them available for reallocation wherever you see fit.
- Players cannot 'loop round' later perks to unlock earlier ones. An example of this would be the [Smithing](/wiki/Skyrim:Smithing "Skyrim:Smithing") skill tree; on the left-hand side of the circle are light armor perks, on the right are heavy armor perks, meeting in the middle at dragon armor at level 100. Although the dragon armor perk is visibly joined to both the glass armor and daedric armor perks, it is not possible to unlock all 3 without first acquiring all the prerequisite light and heavy armor perks.
- Prior to Patch 1.9, it is only possible for a character to unlock 80 of the 251 skill perks; PC users can use the console command `player.addperk` to unlock any desired perk.

## Skill Advancement

The skill advancement mechanism differs between skills. For example, by selling higher value items to merchants, the player gains experience in their Speech skill. Smithing skill increases have been altered by Patch 1.5, they now increase more depending on value of forged equipment. When using a grindwheel or table, the amount by which the enhanced equipment value goes up defines how much experience is gained for it. With 90 smithing and 100% smithing enchanted gear, enhancing an ebony bow from base quality increases experience almost by an entire level. For more details, see each skill's article.

[Trainers](/wiki/Skyrim:Trainers "Skyrim:Trainers") can help level up a skill for a maximum of five times per character level. Unused training sessions do not carry over to the next level.

For information on how to gain free skill boosts, see [this](/wiki/Skyrim:Free_Skill_Boosts "Skyrim:Free Skill Boosts") page.

## Legendary Skills

The skills menu showing Legendary Skills and broken level cap

[Version 1.9](/wiki/Skyrim:Patch#Version_1.9 "Skyrim:Patch") of the Official Skyrim patch allows skills to be reset to their minimum of level 15 and subsequently retrained to gain further experience, while refunding any perk points allocated to that skill. Being able to gain extra experience this way, by leveling a skill from 15 to 100 twice (or more) instead of once, allows the player to exceed the previous level cap of 81, and eventually gain enough skill perks to have all the perks for all skills, at the cost of their current proficiency in the skill every time it is made "legendary". Each skill can be reset multiple times, and they will be marked with the symbol of the Imperial Dragon and a number indicating how many times it has been reset if done so multiple times. In order to unlock all skill perks, the player needs to reach level 252. For a level 81 player with all skills at 100, this requires skills be reset 147 times (or, on average, 8 or 9 resets of EACH skill - although it is better to reset some skills more often than others, and others only a few times or even not at all), with each skill that was reset brought back to level 100.

Note, however, that if the player ever reaches more than 255 unspent perk points, the number of perk points available rolls over to zero at 256 unspent points and starts over, causing you to lose those points.

Bear some things in mind when making a skill Legendary:

- Gaining extra levels - from regaining skills - can, up to a point, result in monsters that scale to your level getting tougher, while you're temporarily weaker on account of having given up a skill. Make sure you still have the ability to defeat tough foes even if it's a weapon or Armor skill that you reset (e.g. have a powerful follower, or don't reset all your weapon skills at once.)
- You do not regain the ability to re-use leveling books to boost the respective skill, or any other similar one-off level-up rewards.
- If you have learned a spell, you keep that spell, and can thus cast high-level spells at low-level skill, to level up quickly - as long as you have the magicka for it. This applies to Destruction, Conjuration, Restoration, Illusion, Alteration. And of course if you have enchanted gear that reduces spell costs, this still works. Note that Destruction spells require a target, Conjuration spells require the presence of a foe, Alteration requires a thing to be altered, Illusion can require people to trick (including civilians and non-combatants), and Restoration healing spells need to actually heal damage which means that you or somebody nearby have to have been hurt. Undead-turning spells require the presence of an undead - of course this may include you if you are a vampire. Some of the spell skills which are the hardest to reach level 100 in the first place, are the easiest ones to Legendary over and over again if you are properly prepared.
- Knowledge of alchemical properties and enchantments is of course retained. (This also means, no more gaining experience by re-learning an alchemical property, or disenchanting an item, but you already know the good recipes.) You're limited by how many ingredients you can get hold of, so stock up.
- Although armor, block and smithing skills can be reduced to nothing, you obviously still keep the good quality armor you found or made earlier - and all the Health from the previous actual levels you've gained - so you can train up Armor and Block skills very quickly by equipping your best armor and going toe-to-toe with a giant, which of course wasn't possible when trying to level up armor the first time. Going toe-to-toe against a giant with low Armor skills is also a good opportunity to boost Restoration in the process.
- Likewise, weapons and weapon skills (One-handed, Two-handed, Archery). Note that enchantment damage on weapons (+fire, +frost, +shock etc.) does not contribute towards the skill. It appears that increasing a weapon's damage by tempering it, or putting perk points in the weapon skill, does not actually cause the skill to increase any faster: indeed, by doubling the damage output without actually doubling the experience gained, you end up needing to find twice as many enemies if you want to level up against enemies, rather than by training against an essential/regenerating non-hostile target (e.g. Shadowmere, Hadvar, Ralof). So for the most efficient retraining, you want a weapon made of the highest quality material but not tempered or enchanted. "Bound" weapons (classing as Daedric) qualify for this, as do actual daedric, ebony or dragonbone.
- Losing all the Smithing perks means that you can't improve future weapons to the same degree as before, until you regain the skill level and perks. (And all those iron building materials that you made for the "Hearthfire" homes don't need to be made a second time.) Jewelry, of course, is unaffected by this, since it requires no perks: and you are free to stock up as many ore ingots as you wish to use in regaining skill levels. Stocking up on high quality Fortify Smithing potions helps give more skill xp from tempering, but not from initially forging a weapon or making jewelry.
- Lockpicking has the awkward feature that if you have already picked a given lock, but it has since reset to locked (e.g. a house overnight, or a door or chest in a dungeon that has respawned after clearing), you do not get experience for picking that lock a second time. So it is possible, and eventually inevitable, to actually run out of locks to pick that will actually improve your skill. Even the training locks in the Thieves Guild are subject to this: and once this hits, you eventually get to a place where Lockpicking can only be boosted by paying gold for training (limited to 5x per level) or breaking lockpicks while failing to pick a lock. Failing to pick a lock with the Skeleton Key gives no experience, since the Skeleton Key does not break... Thus, Lockpicking is probably better to keep at 100 and never make it legendary at all, or at least not more than once (there are enough locks in the game to level Lockpicking up to 100 at least twice, maybe three times if you really cast around and have all the expansions).
- A lot of pickpocketable items do not respawn in the pockets of people around the kingdom: so you can likewise run low on pockets to pick when trying to level it a second time. There is, however, always the option of paying for training (in any skill, doesn't even have to be pickpocketing) and pickpocketing the gold back, or indeed of doing "fishing" (pickpocket) jobs for Delvin Mallory in the [Thieves Guild](/wiki/Skyrim:Thieves_Guild_(faction) "Skyrim:Thieves Guild (faction)"), since this creates items in the target's pockets to be picked. The latter is reliable but can be a bit slow because of all the travelling involved. Leveling Pickpocket up to 100 a second time should be entirely possible.
- A merchant who has been invested in with the "Investor" perk does not lose that investment when you lose the perk, they retain the higher amount of gold even when you no longer have the perk. Conversely, you cannot invest with them a second time after re-leveling Speech to a high enough level to re-gain the perk. However, losing the Merchant and Fence perks removes the ability to sell any item, or stolen items, to any merchant: so you will have to re-allocate points to these perks when your Speech gets back to the appropriate level.
- All the various Speech challenges (persuade/intimidate/bribe) can usually only be done once - the few exceptions (other than bribing/persuading respawning guards to ignore a crime) are glitches, mostly fixed by the Unofficial Patch. If you decide to make Speech legendary, chances are that your only way of regaining the experience is buying and selling items, and that's going to be a LOT of gold value of items bought and sold. High level Alchemy and Smithing are essential for producing such items to sell, as is setting up all the Thieves Guild fences in advance since they have a much higher gold max.
  - Especially if you haven't exploited the synergy of Fortify Alchemy/Enchant/Restoration to make gear with stats and value in the millions. Of course if you \*have\* exploited that glitch, it's possible to have glitched Fortify Enchant+Smithing potions and Fortify Alchemy+Smithing equipment to be able to boost Alchemy and Smithing from 15 to 100 in one go, then sell an item created that way to boost Speech from 15 to 100 in one go. Though this has been fixed by the Unofficial Skyrim Patch, in both Legendary and Special Editions. Without this exploit, it may be a better policy \*not\* to make Speech legendary - especially considering the loss (albeit temporary) of the Merchant and Fence perks: if you want to do it, do it just once.
- Since Enchanting skill gains are based only on the number of items enchanted, or soul gems used to recharge depleted items, leveling Enchanting is no different the second time to the first. Even potions of Fortify Enchant don't affect the skill gains. Stocking up on filled soul gems and items to enchant, is what you need.
- Sneak is likewise pretty much exactly the same to level up a second or subsequent time, as it was the first time round. It's just easier to do once you know where to find the right kind of situation to train sneaking.
- Several perks are applied permanently, even if the related skill is reset and the perk points are returned. These are: [Golden Touch](/wiki/Skyrim:Golden_Touch_(perk) "Skyrim:Golden Touch (perk)"), [Investor](/wiki/Skyrim:Investor "Skyrim:Investor"), [Master of the Mind](/wiki/Skyrim:Master_of_the_Mind "Skyrim:Master of the Mind"), [Master Trader](/wiki/Skyrim:Master_Trader "Skyrim:Master Trader"), [Persuasion](/wiki/Skyrim:Persuasion "Skyrim:Persuasion"), [Ranger](/wiki/Skyrim:Ranger_(perk) "Skyrim:Ranger (perk)"), [Treasure Hunter](/wiki/Skyrim:Treasure_Hunter_(perk) "Skyrim:Treasure Hunter (perk)"), and [Quick Reflexes](/wiki/Skyrim:Quick_Reflexes "Skyrim:Quick Reflexes") [*verification needed — are there more?*]. Consider spending perks points to unlock these *before* resetting your skill.

## Achievements

[Achievements](/wiki/Skyrim:Achievements "Skyrim:Achievements") related to skills are:

-  **[Artificer](/wiki/Skyrim:Artificer "Skyrim:Artificer")** (10 points/Bronze) — Make a [smithed](/wiki/Skyrim:Smithing "Skyrim:Smithing") item, an [enchanted](/wiki/Skyrim:Enchanting "Skyrim:Enchanting") item, and a [potion](/wiki/Skyrim:Alchemy "Skyrim:Alchemy")
-  **[Reader](/wiki/Skyrim:Reader "Skyrim:Reader")** (20 points/Bronze) — Read 50 [Skill Books](/wiki/Skyrim:Skill_Books "Skyrim:Skill Books")
-  **[Thief](/wiki/Skyrim:Thief_(achievement) "Skyrim:Thief (achievement)")** (30 points/Silver) — Pick 50 [locks](/wiki/Skyrim:Lockpicking "Skyrim:Lockpicking") and 50 [pockets](/wiki/Skyrim:Pickpocket "Skyrim:Pickpocket")
-  **[Skill Master](/wiki/Skyrim:Skill_Master "Skyrim:Skill Master")** (40 points/Silver) — Get a skill to 100
-  **[Snake Tongue](/wiki/Skyrim:Snake_Tongue "Skyrim:Snake Tongue")** (10 points/Bronze) — Successfully [persuade](/wiki/Skyrim:Speech "Skyrim:Speech"), bribe, and intimidate

## Notes

- When pending a character level increase, leveling up skills will add to the progress bar of the next level.
- In the skills menu, the nebulae in the backgrounds of the three different categories of skills have the shape of the correspondent category: a mage for the magic skills, a thief for the stealth skills, and a warrior for the combat skills.
- Some quests are only offered to characters who have certain sufficiently developed skills, specifically, the quests given by mages of the [College of Winterhold](/wiki/Skyrim:College_of_Winterhold_(faction) "Skyrim:College of Winterhold (faction)") when you have reached a skill level of 90 or 100 in one of the five schools of magic.
- Increasing developed skills leads to faster character level increases.
- Faster skill increases are possible by activating certain [Standing Stones](/wiki/Skyrim:Standing_Stone "Skyrim:Standing Stone").
  - Even though Archery is considered a Combat Skill, Thief Stone enhances the skill gain in Archery, not Warrior Stone.
- If you are using a potion or spell that modifies one or more of the skills, making those skills Legendary will cause those modified skills to not level up again. To fix this, be sure that the spell effect has expired, so that the skill being reset will default back to their normal start level. To be sure you have it set correctly, the skill level should appear in white, instead of the green or red used for modified levels. [*verification needed — Is this a bug?*]
- Because Skyrim does not have classes, the distinction between major and minor skills from previous Elder Scrolls games does not exist any more — characters do not have a predetermined list of skills that increase more quickly.
- [Skills from Oblivion](/wiki/Oblivion:Skills "Oblivion:Skills") that have been removed without a singularly-defined replacement include:
  - Armorer: Weapons and armor no longer require repair, though [smithing](/wiki/Skyrim:Smithing "Skyrim:Smithing") allows the player to improve these items and create new weapons and armor.
  - Athletics and Acrobatics: Running, jumping, and swimming ability are now based entirely on [race](/wiki/Skyrim:Races "Skyrim:Races") though you can sprint longer with more stamina.
  - Blade and Blunt: Weapon skills are instead divided into [One-handed](/wiki/Skyrim:One-handed "Skyrim:One-handed") and [Two-handed](/wiki/Skyrim:Two-handed "Skyrim:Two-handed") skills. Perks within those skills allow you to specialize in certain weapon types.
  - Hand to Hand: No true replacement, although various features enhance unarmed combat ([Khajiit](/wiki/Skyrim:Khajiit "Skyrim:Khajiit") have claw attacks; a [Heavy Armor perk](/wiki/Skyrim:Heavy_Armor#Fists_of_Steel "Skyrim:Heavy Armor") increases hand-to-hand damage; an enchantment effect for increased hand-to-hand damage exists via the [Gloves of the Pugilist](/wiki/Skyrim:Gloves_of_the_Pugilist "Skyrim:Gloves of the Pugilist") and [gauntlets](/wiki/Skyrim:Fearsome_Fists_Items "Skyrim:Fearsome Fists Items") added by the [Fearsome Fists](/wiki/Skyrim:Fearsome_Fists "Skyrim:Fearsome Fists") [Creation](/wiki/Skyrim:Creation_Club "Skyrim:Creation Club").)
  - Mercantile and Speechcraft: Combined into the [Speech](/wiki/Skyrim:Speech "Skyrim:Speech") skill.
  - Mysticism: Spells shifted to other magic skills
- [Skills from Oblivion](/wiki/Oblivion:Skills "Oblivion:Skills") that have been renamed:
  - Marksman: Replaced with [Archery](/wiki/Skyrim:Archery "Skyrim:Archery")
  - Security: Replaced with [Lockpicking](/wiki/Skyrim:Lockpicking "Skyrim:Lockpicking")
- Skills from pre-Oblivion games that have returned:
  - [Morrowind](/wiki/Morrowind:Skills "Morrowind:Skills")'s [Enchant](/wiki/Morrowind:Enchant "Morrowind:Enchant") returns as [Enchanting](/wiki/Skyrim:Enchanting "Skyrim:Enchanting").
  - [Daggerfall](/wiki/Daggerfall:Skills "Daggerfall:Skills")'s Pickpocket returns as [Pickpocket](/wiki/Skyrim:Pickpocket "Skyrim:Pickpocket").

Skuldafn

**Skuldafn** is a large [Nordic ruin](/wiki/Skyrim:Nordic_Ruins "Skyrim:Nordic Ruins") with a portal to [Sovngarde](/wiki/Skyrim:Sovngarde_(place) "Skyrim:Sovngarde (place)") containing [draugr](/wiki/Skyrim:Draugr "Skyrim:Draugr"), [dragons](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon "Skyrim:Dragon"), and a [dragon priest](/wiki/Skyrim:Nahkriin_(creature) "Skyrim:Nahkriin (creature)"). It contains four interior zones, two of which are unconnected: *[Skuldafn Temple](#Skuldafn_Temple)*, a second *[Skuldafn Temple](#Skuldafn_Temple_2)*, *[Skuldafn South Tower](#Skuldafn_South_Tower)*, and *[Skuldafn North Tower](#Skuldafn_North_Tower)*, with a separate *[exterior](#Exterior:_Skuldafn_Temple)* area behind the temple.

The only way to reach Skuldafn is by forcing [Odahviing](/wiki/Skyrim:Odahviing "Skyrim:Odahviing") to fly you there; this is accomplished during the quest [The Fallen](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Fallen "Skyrim:The Fallen"). He will fly away after leaving you there. The only way to leave Skuldafn is to take the portal to the [Nordic afterlife](/wiki/Skyrim:Sovngarde_(place) "Skyrim:Sovngarde (place)").

## Related Quests

- **[The World-Eater's Eyrie](/wiki/Skyrim:The_World-Eater%27s_Eyrie "Skyrim:The World-Eater's Eyrie")**: Battle through Skuldafn to reach [Alduin](/wiki/Skyrim:Alduin "Skyrim:Alduin")'s portal to [Sovngarde](/wiki/Skyrim:Sovngarde_(place) "Skyrim:Sovngarde (place)").

### Exterior

Skuldafn overview

Odahviing will drop you off on top of an old dragon mound. You should be facing east, toward a low arch which opens to a stone bridge over a shallow lake. Just to the right before the arch is a tree stump with [mora tapinella](/wiki/Skyrim:Mora_Tapinella "Skyrim:Mora Tapinella") growing on it. There is a draugr on either side of the far end of the bridge, another draugr patrolling the stairs off to the far right, and a dragon constantly circling overhead.

Beyond the far end of the bridge to the left is a [blue mountain flower](/wiki/Skyrim:Blue_Mountain_Flower "Skyrim:Blue Mountain Flower"), while to the right is a [purple mountain flower](/wiki/Skyrim:Purple_Mountain_Flower "Skyrim:Purple Mountain Flower"), a [thistle](/wiki/Skyrim:Thistle_Branch "Skyrim:Thistle Branch"), and a [snowberry](/wiki/Skyrim:Snowberries "Skyrim:Snowberries") bush to the left of stairs rising to the south. To the right before these stairs are other stairs descending to the lake, which contains nothing of interest. Along the south edge of the lake is a blue mountain flower and a purple mountain flower, with another purple mountain flower at the north end to the right of the main waterfall feeding the lake. Return to the first flight of stairs rising to the south, and you will enter a paved area with another two draugr, one of which is a magic-user. There is another thistle to the right, and a [red mountain flower](/wiki/Skyrim:Red_Mountain_Flower "Skyrim:Red Mountain Flower") to the left.

After this is a large courtyard; when you enter it, another dragon will begin circling overhead. There are more draugr patrolling the battlements to the left, who may detect you if you choose to fight the dragon here. There is a snowberry bush just to the left of where you enter the courtyard, and a purple mountain flower farther along the wall. There is a red mountain flower at the base of the left flight of stairs rising to the east, a snowberry bush at the base of the right flight of stairs, a thistle in the middle of the courtyard, and another red mountain flower near a tree stump with mora tapinella growing on it to the west. The entrance to *[Skuldafn South Tower](#Skuldafn_South_Tower)* is on the south side of the courtyard.

At the top of the stairs, on a walkway above is a patrolling draugr. Heading forward, there is a ruined tower to the left; it contains a [chest](/wiki/Skyrim:Chest "Skyrim:Chest") on the second level. There is a draugr patrolling the next area to the north, another watching the area from the broken stairs farther to the north, two more walking along the higher walkway to the west, and two more on the higher walkway to the east. Once all of these draugr are dealt with, proceed to the south along the walkways. There is an altar here with three draugr; two are patrolling the lower area, and one is guarding the raised area with the altar, on top of which is a chest. To the east of the altar is the door to *[Skuldafn North Tower](#Skuldafn_North_Tower)*. Before you enter *Skuldafn Temple* back to the north, follow the walls to the west and north from the temple entrance, and you will find a chest with a random [potion of healing](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Minor_Healing "Skyrim:Potion of Minor Healing"), [magicka](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Minor_Magicka "Skyrim:Potion of Minor Magicka"), or [stamina](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Minor_Stamina "Skyrim:Potion of Minor Stamina") beside it. If you look up, you should see a short wooden bridge connecting the tower in front of you to the second exterior area behind the temple.

### Skuldafn Temple

In keeping with the general theme of the place, the temple is rather large. There is an [urn](/wiki/Skyrim:Urn "Skyrim:Urn") in front, another to the left, and an altar with two random [poisons](/wiki/Skyrim:Poisons "Skyrim:Poisons") on top to the right. The first room may appear deserted, but there are three draugr waiting toward the rear of the room behind the central raised section. Both paths pass under bridges that link this raised area with the sides of the chamber, and both lead to the same place. The path on the right is strewn with rubble, but contains a chest, while the path on the left is trapped, with two [pressure plates](/wiki/Skyrim:Traps#Pressure_Plate "Skyrim:Traps") along the path that cause a series of [dart traps](/wiki/Skyrim:Traps#Dart_Trap "Skyrim:Traps") to trigger from both walls. In the area with the three draugr is another altar with two [burial urns](/wiki/Skyrim:Burial_Urn "Skyrim:Burial Urn") on top and four more on the ground around it.

After dispatching these first draugr, continue up the stairs; again, both lead to the same area. There is a magic-using draugr in the next room, while another four slumber in sarcophagi to the sides. One on each side will emerge as you reach the top of the stairs, while the other two will emerge once you pass the three rotating pillars in the middle of the room. Once these draugr are out of the way, take a moment to assess the puzzle. There are two solutions here for two gates; the two side pillars face outwards, while the one in the middle faces the gates. The right gate's solution, from east to west, is **[Snake—Eagle—Whale](/wiki/Skyrim:Puzzles#Spinning_Symbol.2FRune_Totems "Skyrim:Puzzles")**, and the left gate's solution, again from east to west, is **[Snake—Snake—Whale](/wiki/Skyrim:Puzzles#Spinning_Symbol.2FRune_Totems "Skyrim:Puzzles")**. Pull the lever to activate each solution and raise the corresponding gate; raising the second gate will not lower the first.

There is a cave-in behind the right gate with a chest among the rubble, while to the left of the left gate is another urn, and the path continues beyond this gate. Once past the gate there is a cave-in directly ahead, with a flight of stairs rising to the west. The passage leads out onto a balcony overlooking a small room containing a magic-using draugr standing in front of an altar. There are two flights of stairs descending into the room on either side of a large statue. However, as you begin to descend the stairs, two more draugr burst from sarcophagi: one at the back of the room behind the altar, and the other on the balcony off to the right. Directly under the statue is a chest, and on the altar is a mummified [draugr corpse](/wiki/Skyrim:Containers#Draugr "Skyrim:Containers") and three burial urns. When the sarcophagus on the west wall burst open, it revealed an opening in the back.

Beyond this opening, you'll see a large amount of cobwebs and spider egg sacs. You'll also be able to hear several [frostbite spiders](/wiki/Skyrim:Frostbite_Spider "Skyrim:Frostbite Spider") moving around. You will need to hack or burn through the webbing into catacombs infested with the spiders, with a series of burial alcoves along both walls. The catacombs rise to the north, where another section has caved in. There are three [egg sacs](/wiki/Skyrim:Egg_Sac "Skyrim:Egg Sac") from which you can harvest [spider eggs](/wiki/Skyrim:Spider_Egg "Skyrim:Spider Egg") among the fallen masonry. There is a doorway to the east covered with more cobwebs you'll need to hack or burn through. Beyond this doorway is a narrow passage that first turns north and climbs more stairs, before turning east again with yet more stairs leading up. There is a frostbite spider near the top of the first flight, and two more at the top in a wider section of the passage in front of a pair of iron doors. There is a blocked passage on the right containing another egg sac and a chest hidden beneath thick cobwebs you'll need to hack or burn through. On the floor to the right of the doors is a [salt pile](/wiki/Skyrim:Salt_Pile "Skyrim:Salt Pile").

Beyond the doors is a room with a raised central section and balconies on both sides linked by a pair of walkways crossing above the lower level. Two draugr in this room patrol both balconies and the raised central section. There is a pillar puzzle here; the solution, from north to south, is **[Whale—Snake—Eagle](/wiki/Skyrim:Puzzles#Spinning_Symbol.2FRune_Totems "Skyrim:Puzzles")**. You can also use the [Whirlwind Sprint](/wiki/Skyrim:Whirlwind_Sprint "Skyrim:Whirlwind Sprint") [shout](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Shouts "Skyrim:Dragon Shouts") to reach the exit to the east from the raised central section. The first pillar is immediately in front of you when you enter the room; this is the "middle" pillar, and should be turned so the snake shows. On the lower level there is an urn to the north and a chest to the east behind the central section. The symbol for the middle totem can also be seen at the rear of the room. The other symbols are high above the walkways on either side of the room. There are stairs to the south leading up to the balcony and the third pillar, which should be turned so the eagle shows. Head across the walkways, past the lever with many skulls lying around it, to the "first" pillar, which should be turned so the whale shows. Once this is done, pull the lever and a raised wooden bridge will fall into place from the east, granting access to a pair of iron doors and an urn on either side of the bridge. Go through the doors to the second *Skuldafn Temple* zone.

### Skuldafn Temple

Around the corner to the north is a split-level room containing three draugr, with one on the lower level and two above. There is an empty chest on an altar in front of the draugr on the lower level. The path forward is up a flight of stairs at the back of the room, then to the right, which cuts back to a bridge over the altar. Once across the bridge, there's a doorway into a wider passage that turns north after a few paces. At the far end is another doorway into a room with a pressure plate on the floor which activates a double trap. The first part of the trap is highly visible when triggered, with a lantern dropping onto and igniting an [oil slick](/wiki/Skyrim:Traps#Oil_Slicks.2FOil_Lanterns "Skyrim:Traps"). The second part of the trap is a dart trap on the opposite wall. There is a wooden spiral staircase in the middle of the room. On your left is a sideboard holding a burial urn and a skull with a [flawless garnet](/wiki/Skyrim:Flawless_Garnet "Skyrim:Flawless Garnet") on top. To the right of the sideboard is an urn, and against the back wall is a set of shelves holding an empty random [soul gem](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Gems "Skyrim:Soul Gems"), a random potion of stamina, and a sack, with a burial urn on the floor beside it.

At the top of the staircase is a room with a closed gate to the north, and a closed pair of iron doors to the south, with a window on either side of the doors. Looking through the windows, you will see a draugr in the small room beyond the doors. There is another draugr slumbering in a sarcophagus in the same small room, which will burst open when you enter the room. In the small room, there is an oil slick on the floor, an oil lantern hanging above, a chest to the right, and the lever to raise the closed gate to the left.

The passage beyond the gate rises, passing an urn before turning east by more fallen masonry. The next wide corridor has two pressure plates along it that drop another oil lantern onto an oil slick. One of the plates is in front of a chest on the right, and the other is in the middle of the corridor to the left of the chest. At the far end of the corridor are some skeletal remains beside an [iron battleaxe](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Battleaxe "Skyrim:Iron Battleaxe"). At this point the passage turns back to the north, and another wide corridor leads past an urn to a [puzzle door](/wiki/Skyrim:Puzzles#Dragon_Claw_Switch "Skyrim:Puzzles") guarded by a high-level draugr or even a [dragon priest](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Priest "Skyrim:Dragon Priest"). The draugr carries the [Diamond Claw](/wiki/Skyrim:Diamond_Claw "Skyrim:Diamond Claw"), which reveals the combination for the door, from top to bottom, as **[Fox—Moth—Dragon](/wiki/Skyrim:Puzzles#Dragon_Claw_Switch "Skyrim:Puzzles")**. Beyond the door is a short flight of stairs leading up to a huge chamber, with the [word wall](/wiki/Skyrim:Word_Wall "Skyrim:Word Wall") at the far end of a wide path with thrones on either side. On the first two thrones are lootable [skeletons](/wiki/Skyrim:Skeleton "Skyrim:Skeleton"). The word wall teaches part of the [Storm Call](/wiki/Skyrim:Storm_Call "Skyrim:Storm Call") shout.

Continue to the left of the wall, past a [burnt corpse](/wiki/Skyrim:Containers#Burnt_Corpse "Skyrim:Containers") and an [iron greatsword](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Greatsword "Skyrim:Iron Greatsword"). Climb the stairs and follow the passage north, which turns west before a doorway to a room to the north. The room contains a stone table holding a draugr corpse, two random potions of healing, magicka, or stamina, a random [war axe](/wiki/Skyrim:War_Axe "Skyrim:War Axe"), a random [helmet](/wiki/Skyrim:Helmet "Skyrim:Helmet"), and a burial urn. Beside the table on the floor is a second burial urn, with an urn to the left of the table. A set of shelves on the east side of the room holds three more burial urns, a random [potion of regeneration](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Regeneration "Skyrim:Potion of Regeneration"), and a stone bowl containing a [flawless diamond](/wiki/Skyrim:Flawless_Diamond "Skyrim:Flawless Diamond"), a [flawless emerald](/wiki/Skyrim:Flawless_Emerald "Skyrim:Flawless Emerald"), and a [flawless amethyst](/wiki/Skyrim:Flawless_Amethyst "Skyrim:Flawless Amethyst") hidden under a linen wrap. At the end of the passage is a pair of iron doors leading to *Skuldafn Temple Exterior*.

### Exterior: Skuldafn Temple

When you emerge, at least two draugr will immediately notice your presence. Deal with them, and head straight ahead from the temple exit to the tower connected by a short wooden bridge that was visible from outside the first entrance to the temple. Head down a level to find a set of shelves and a sideboard holding two random potions of healing, magicka, or stamina, a honed or standard ancient Nord sword or war axe, and a flawless emerald. There is also an urn on this level. There is a ramp leading down on the outside of the tower to the lower levels, where you will find an urn and a chest. Be careful not to fall down here; if you survive, you will need to traverse the whole temple again. Return to the top level of the tower and the area outside the temple exit, and proceed to the south and east to two draugr guarding a flight of stairs rising to the north.

If you have attempted to [sneak](/wiki/Skyrim:Sneak "Skyrim:Sneak") in this area, you may have noticed you are being detected, but not attacked. If you look to the top of the stairs, you will see a dragon looking back. This dragon, and another on the opposite side of the portal which is also visible at the top of the stairs, are not aggressive. Continue up the stairs, where the dragon priest [Nahkriin](/wiki/Skyrim:Nahkriin_(creature) "Skyrim:Nahkriin (creature)") awaits. He has a decent amount of [magic resistance](/wiki/Skyrim:Magic_Resistance "Skyrim:Magic Resistance") and a small amount of physical resistance, and knows many spells, including summoning, ward, wall, and cloak spells. He also has perks granting greater magic and healing effects to his spells. Once he has been defeated, loot him for his eponymous [mask](/wiki/Skyrim:Nahkriin_(item) "Skyrim:Nahkriin (item)") and his [staff](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Priest_Staff_(Nahkriin) "Skyrim:Dragon Priest Staff (Nahkriin)"), which is needed to access [Sovngarde](/wiki/Skyrim:Sovngarde_(place) "Skyrim:Sovngarde (place)"). You can choose to fight the two unaggressive dragons for their loot and souls at this point. Attacking one of them will turn both hostile. One generally uses frost breath, while the other uses fire breath. They will repeat the phrase *"Skuldafn fen kos dinok"* while attacking you.

When you are ready, ascend to the small platform overlooking the area where the portal had been prior to the battle. Activate the dragon seal by placing Nahkriin's staff in it, then enter the portal to exit Skuldafn and enter the Nordic afterlife of Sovngarde.

### Skuldafn South Tower

The tower is quite small, but still populated by draugr. Before ascending the spiral ramp, check the room to your right. There are two draugr in here, and an urn. There is another draugr patrolling the ramp. There are two more draugr guarding a chest and an urn in the room at the top of the ramp. The doors to the southeast and southwest exit the building. You emerge high above the entrance, but can jump down to the protrusion over the entrance and then jump safely to the ground.

### Skuldafn North Tower

The tower is quite small, but still populated by draugr. Before ascending the spiral ramp, check the room to your right. There is a single draugr in here. There is another draugr patrolling the ramp. There is one more draugr guarding a chest in the room at the top of the ramp. The door to the southwest exits the building. You emerge high above the entrance, but can jump down to the protrusion over the entrance and then jump safely to the ground. Before you do so, enter the other door to discover another chest hidden among the rubble in the southeast tip of the interior.

## Notes

- It is possible to enter Sovngarde without obtaining Nahkriin's staff if you reach the open portal quickly enough.
- Skuldafn is only accessible during the related quest, and it is impossible to return to the location after you enter the portal to Sovngarde, so be sure to get everything you want from the area before you enter the portal. Nahkriin's mask is required to get the ninth dragon priest mask, [Konahrik](/wiki/Skyrim:Konahrik "Skyrim:Konahrik"), so be sure to loot him. If you missed them, it is possible to recover Nahkriin's mask and the word of the Storm Call shout while maintaining your progress without using mods or console commands by using the [Dead Loading glitch](/wiki/Skyrim:Glitches#Dead_Loading "Skyrim:Glitches").
- All four dragons in Skuldafn are unique. The difference between ordinary dragons and the first two dragons in Skuldafn is that the latter have the [dunSkuldafnDragonFaction](/wiki/Skyrim:DunSkuldafnDragonFaction "Skyrim:DunSkuldafnDragonFaction") so they don't fight the draugr in the area, and their displayed name will always be "Dragon". The two dragons by the portal are unaggressive versions of the first two, but will fight you if you attack them. All four may have higher stats than the ordinary versions of their type.
- If [Durnehviir](/wiki/Skyrim:Durnehviir_(dragon) "Skyrim:Durnehviir (dragon)")[DG](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard") is summoned in Skuldafn, he will also speak the unique dialogue that the other dragons in the area have while in combat.
- This location is where Alduin flies off to at the beginning of the game. It is possible to chase him all the way into the mountains and spot him circling the Skuldafn region of the Tamriel worldspace.
- [Fast travel](/wiki/Skyrim:Fast_Travel "Skyrim:Fast Travel") is not available in Skuldafn.
- The [Clear Skies](/wiki/Skyrim:Clear_Skies "Skyrim:Clear Skies") shout is not effective in Skuldafn.
- The [Bend Will](/wiki/Skyrim:Bend_Will "Skyrim:Bend Will")[DB](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonborn "Skyrim:Dragonborn") shout is not effective on the dragons in Skuldafn.
- Skuldafn also [appears](/wiki/Online:Skuldafn "Online:Skuldafn") in [ESO](/wiki/Online:Online "Online:Online").

## Bugs

- If the puzzle door does not work, check [here](/wiki/Skyrim:Puzzles#Bugs "Skyrim:Puzzles") for possible fixes.
- If you kill Nahkriin while hidden and he is atop the rise (with a bow, for example), he may not drop his staff, and you will then be unable to unlock the portal to Sovngarde.
- One of the draugr near an altar may act peaceful and not attack at all.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.0.8, addresses this issue. The draugr had the amush script and was initially docile. This was obviously wrong for one that doesn't use a crypt. It has been replaced with an aggressive warlock version.

# Skyrim:Sky Haven Temple

## Overview

Sky Haven Temple

**Sky Haven Temple** is a large mountaintop fort that served as the major [Blades](/wiki/Skyrim:Blades "Skyrim:Blades") temple and outpost in [Skyrim](/wiki/Skyrim:Skyrim "Skyrim:Skyrim"), now long abandoned and in [Forsworn](/wiki/Skyrim:Forsworn "Skyrim:Forsworn") territory. It has a long and rich history as the Blades' main base in Skyrim. According to [Esbern](/wiki/Skyrim:Esbern "Skyrim:Esbern"), the temple has been abandoned for thousands of years, although the date it was last in use by the Blades is unknown. After it has been reclaimed by acting Grandmaster [Delphine](/wiki/Skyrim:Delphine "Skyrim:Delphine"), she will attempt to rebuild the Blades, using it as a hidden base of operations.

It is also the long-forgotten location of [Alduin's Wall](/wiki/Lore:Alduin%27s_Wall "Lore:Alduin's Wall"), a pictorial repository of ancient [Akaviri](/wiki/Lore:Akaviri "Lore:Akaviri") dragonlore, including all the information ever gathered regarding [Alduin](/wiki/Skyrim:Alduin "Skyrim:Alduin"), the [Dragon Cult](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Cult "Skyrim:Dragon Cult"), and their reign of terror. It also details a prophecy regarding their defeat. The last panel speaks of Alduin's return and his contending with the last [Dragonborn](/wiki/Skyrim:Dovahkiin "Skyrim:Dovahkiin") at the end of time. More information on the history of the temple and Alduin's Wall can be found on the [lore page](/wiki/Lore:Sky_Haven_Temple "Lore:Sky Haven Temple").

The temple can only be accessed once stage 30 of the quest [Alduin's Wall](/wiki/Skyrim:Alduin%27s_Wall "Skyrim:Alduin's Wall") has been reached. It is possible to discover the map marker beforehand, thus skipping the Forsworn and puzzles in the [Karthspire](/wiki/Skyrim:Karthspire "Skyrim:Karthspire"), by fast traveling during the quest, but entry to the temple will be impossible. The temple includes an interior, *[Sky Haven Temple](#Sky_Haven_Temple)*, and an [exterior](#Exterior) courtyard at the top of the Karthspire mountain. The interior consists of sleeping quarters, a dining hall, and a small armory. The courtyard is used to watch over the surrounding area and for training purposes.

When you and Delphine have reclaimed the temple as the new headquarters of the Blades, you can bring up to three [followers](/wiki/Skyrim:Followers "Skyrim:Followers") back to her and have them inducted into the Blades. Esbern offers the [Dragonslayer's Blessing](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonslayer%27s_Blessing "Skyrim:Dragonslayer's Blessing") (stackable with divine blessings) that lasts for five days, giving you a greatly increased chance of critical hits against [dragons](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon "Skyrim:Dragon"), and will tell you about his [dragon research](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Research "Skyrim:Dragon Research"), eventually offering a potion that grants the [Dragon Infusion](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Infusion "Skyrim:Dragon Infusion") [ability](/wiki/Skyrim:Powers "Skyrim:Powers"), which causes you to take less damage from dragons. He will also offer the services of all the newly recruited Blades to aid you in [hunting a dragon](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Hunting "Skyrim:Dragon Hunting") at a random [dragon lair](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Lairs "Skyrim:Dragon Lairs").

If you fast travel to Sky Haven Temple after discovering it, you will actually land inside the Karthspire, in front of the door to the temple near the blood seal.

## Residents

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| | Sky Haven Temple | | --- | | **[Delphine](/wiki/Skyrim:Delphine "Skyrim:Delphine")**  **[Esbern](/wiki/Skyrim:Esbern "Skyrim:Esbern")** | |

Note: The quest [Rebuilding the Blades](/wiki/Skyrim:Rebuilding_the_Blades "Skyrim:Rebuilding the Blades") allows you to make up to three of your followers into Blades. They will leave their former lives and reside here. If any of them die after becoming a Blade, you cannot replace them.

## Related Quests

Two new recruits relaxing

### Main Quest

- **[Alduin's Wall](/wiki/Skyrim:Alduin%27s_Wall "Skyrim:Alduin's Wall")**: Locate the prophecy within Sky Haven Temple.
- **[The Throat of the World](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Throat_of_the_World "Skyrim:The Throat of the World")**: Receive a lesson from [Paarthurnax](/wiki/Skyrim:Paarthurnax_(dragon) "Skyrim:Paarthurnax (dragon)").
- **[Elder Knowledge](/wiki/Skyrim:Elder_Knowledge "Skyrim:Elder Knowledge")**: Recover an [Elder Scroll](/wiki/Skyrim:Elder_Scroll "Skyrim:Elder Scroll") to learn an [Ancient Secret](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonrend "Skyrim:Dragonrend").
- **[The Fallen](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Fallen "Skyrim:The Fallen")**: Capture and interrogate [an ally](/wiki/Skyrim:Odahviing "Skyrim:Odahviing") of [Alduin](/wiki/Skyrim:Alduin "Skyrim:Alduin").
- **[Paarthurnax](/wiki/Skyrim:Paarthurnax_(quest) "Skyrim:Paarthurnax (quest)")**: Deal with a [potential threat](/wiki/Skyrim:Paarthurnax_(dragon) "Skyrim:Paarthurnax (dragon)").

### Blades Quests

- **[Dragon Hunting](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Hunting "Skyrim:Dragon Hunting")**: Kill a [dragon](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon "Skyrim:Dragon") at its [lair](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Lairs "Skyrim:Dragon Lairs").
- **[Dragon Research](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Research "Skyrim:Dragon Research")**: Help [Esbern](/wiki/Skyrim:Esbern "Skyrim:Esbern") complete his research on [dragons](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon "Skyrim:Dragon").
- **[Rebuilding the Blades](/wiki/Skyrim:Rebuilding_the_Blades "Skyrim:Rebuilding the Blades")**: Recruit new members for the [Blades](/wiki/Skyrim:Blades "Skyrim:Blades").

### Exterior

The exterior of Sky Haven temple from the Karthspire

Two separate exterior areas connect to the temple: the cave outside the entrance from the Karthspire, and the courtyard at the top of the mountain. The only distinct features of the Karthspire cave exterior are a stone face covering the entrance, the "blood seal" on the ground before it bearing the Dragonborn symbol, and the large unlocked [chest](/wiki/Skyrim:Chest "Skyrim:Chest") in the center of the cavern with unlit braziers at each corner. There is also a [quicksilver ore vein](/wiki/Skyrim:Quicksilver_Ore_Vein "Skyrim:Quicksilver Ore Vein") on the right-hand wall as you enter this area. See [here](/wiki/Skyrim:Karthspire "Skyrim:Karthspire") for full details of this area and the cave system leading to it.

The courtyard is on top of the mountain and has an impressive field of vision, covering most of the main roads leading to and from [Markarth](/wiki/Skyrim:Markarth "Skyrim:Markarth"). From the courtyard, it is possible to see [Reachwind Eyrie](/wiki/Skyrim:Reachwind_Eyrie "Skyrim:Reachwind Eyrie") to the south, and [Kolskeggr Mine](/wiki/Skyrim:Kolskeggr_Mine "Skyrim:Kolskeggr Mine") to the north. The western view is blocked by part of the mountains in that direction, while the eastern view is blocked by the temple building. By climbing the rocks behind the building, it is possible to see the waterfalls beside [Old Hroldan Inn](/wiki/Skyrim:Old_Hroldan_Inn "Skyrim:Old Hroldan Inn"), [Soljund's Sinkhole](/wiki/Skyrim:Soljund%27s_Sinkhole "Skyrim:Soljund's Sinkhole"), and [Sundered Towers](/wiki/Skyrim:Sundered_Towers "Skyrim:Sundered Towers") to the east, while Markarth to the west is just visible.

There are two open-sided structures outside in the courtyard; one has several [hanging moss](/wiki/Skyrim:Hanging_Moss "Skyrim:Hanging Moss") growing from the roof. Both structures are initially empty.

After returning from the quest [The Throat of the World](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Throat_of_the_World "Skyrim:The Throat of the World"), the first structure will have two archery targets, one raised on a bale of straw, and a practice dummy. The structure with an arched roof will function as a lookout post. When Esbern is found outside, he will stand lookout. When Delphine is outside, she will alternate between training alone, training with each of the Blade recruits, or standing lookout. Any recruits will alternate between training alone, training with Delphine, and wandering about the small area. There are also five trees with [juniper berries](/wiki/Skyrim:Juniper_Berries "Skyrim:Juniper Berries") and a tree stump with [mora tapinella](/wiki/Skyrim:Mora_Tapinella "Skyrim:Mora Tapinella") fungus growing on it around the courtyard. Although it is a fairly small area, it is large enough for a dragon to land, giving the recruits some live targets to train on.

### Sky Haven Temple

Sky Haven Temple's main hall

When you first arrive in the company of Delphine and Esbern, the Temple will be quite dark; a light source is highly recommended. You enter after clearing the puzzles and traps and passing the blood seal in the cave outside. At the top of a few flights of stairs from the door is the main room. This room is quite large, and contains the main object of interest, **Alduin's Wall**, which prophesies the Dragonborn's [fate](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonslayer "Skyrim:Dragonslayer"). Esbern will immediately rush over to it and start to inspect it while muttering to himself. This large room serves as the dining room, gathering room, and Esbern's study. In the middle of the lower part of the room is a very long, empty stone dining table, with a smaller, empty wooden table.

Esbern will set up his study to the right-hand side of the wall, and as the [main quest](/wiki/Skyrim:Main_Quest "Skyrim:Main Quest") progresses, more books will be added to his table and bookcase. Most of his books are about dragons or the Dragonborn prophecy, and although he mentions a library in the Temple, one does not exist in-game.

The multitude of stairs in the hall can be quite confusing. From the entrance, the left-hand and central stairs lead to the main room, while the right-hand stairs lead to the side of the same room and a set of stairs to the level above Alduin's Wall. The stairs in the northwest corner of the main room split: the left-hand fork leads to the front of the sleeping quarters, while the right-hand fork leads to halfway between the sleeping quarters and the area above the wall. The three sets of stairs in the area above the wall all lead to another small area containing five separate doors, all of which lead to the courtyard at the top of the mountain.

The sleeping quarters in the northwestern corner initially contains seven unlocked chests containing minor loot, an empty set of shelves, five unowned single beds, and an old extinguished campfire. In the middle of the room are four chairs and two empty wooden tables, one small and square and the other longer, as well as two food barrels beside a pillar.

The stone dining table in the main hall points almost directly at the armory to the west. On the wooden table in the armory is [Dragonbane](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragonbane "Skyrim:Dragonbane") (a one-handed Akaviri katana), an [iron dagger](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Dagger "Skyrim:Iron Dagger"), an [iron mace](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Mace "Skyrim:Iron Mace"), and the [One-handed](/wiki/Skyrim:One-handed "Skyrim:One-handed") [skill book](/wiki/Skyrim:Skill_Books "Skyrim:Skill Books") *[Mace Etiquette](/wiki/Skyrim:Mace_Etiquette "Skyrim:Mace Etiquette")*. Hanging on the wall to the left are six [Blades swords](/wiki/Skyrim:Blades_Sword "Skyrim:Blades Sword"), and between the wall and table is an unlocked chest containing all five pieces of the [Blades equipment](/wiki/Skyrim:Specialty_Gear#Blades_Equipment "Skyrim:Specialty Gear") and some [coins](/wiki/Skyrim:Gold "Skyrim:Gold").

Once you have completed the quest The Throat of the World and return to the temple, you will find that the braziers have all been lit, casting slightly more light, but still leaving large areas in darkness. There are now rugs scattered on the floor throughout. The long stone table in the main chamber containing Alduin's Wall now holds an [iron greatsword](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Greatsword "Skyrim:Iron Greatsword"), two bottles of [alto wine](/wiki/Skyrim:Alto_Wine "Skyrim:Alto Wine"), a bottle of [wine](/wiki/Skyrim:Wine "Skyrim:Wine"), two bottles of [Nord mead](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord_Mead "Skyrim:Nord Mead"), a [cabbage](/wiki/Skyrim:Cabbage "Skyrim:Cabbage"), a [salmon steak](/wiki/Skyrim:Salmon_Steak "Skyrim:Salmon Steak"), a [potato](/wiki/Skyrim:Potato "Skyrim:Potato"), a sprig of [snowberries](/wiki/Skyrim:Snowberries "Skyrim:Snowberries"), several loaves of [bread](/wiki/Skyrim:Bread "Skyrim:Bread"), and a wedge of cheese among fine crockery. Three chairs are arranged along either side of the table. To the left of the wall is a long wooden table and chair with various [arms](/wiki/Skyrim:Weapons "Skyrim:Weapons") and [armor](/wiki/Skyrim:Armor "Skyrim:Armor"), including an [iron helmet](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Helmet "Skyrim:Iron Helmet"), a [banded iron shield](/wiki/Skyrim:Banded_Iron_Shield "Skyrim:Banded Iron Shield"), a [hunting bow](/wiki/Skyrim:Hunting_Bow "Skyrim:Hunting Bow"), a [steel mace](/wiki/Skyrim:Steel_Mace "Skyrim:Steel Mace"), a [dwarven sword](/wiki/Skyrim:Dwarven_Sword "Skyrim:Dwarven Sword"), an [iron war axe](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_War_Axe "Skyrim:Iron War Axe"), and two loose [iron arrows](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Arrow "Skyrim:Iron Arrow"). On the floor to the left is a [grindstone](/wiki/Skyrim:Grindstone "Skyrim:Grindstone").

The table and bookcase to the right of the wall is where Esbern can normally be found studying. On the table is a [salt pile](/wiki/Skyrim:Salt_Pile "Skyrim:Salt Pile"), a [garlic](/wiki/Skyrim:Garlic "Skyrim:Garlic") bulb, several rolls of paper, and copies of *[The Book of the Dragonborn](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Book_of_the_Dragonborn "Skyrim:The Book of the Dragonborn")* and a complete set of *[Brief History of the Empire](/wiki/Skyrim:Brief_History_of_the_Empire "Skyrim:Brief History of the Empire")* volumes 1–4. To the right is a set of shelves holding eleven [common books](/wiki/Skyrim:Books "Skyrim:Books") and several rarer or unique books including *[Atlas of Dragons](/wiki/Skyrim:Atlas_of_Dragons "Skyrim:Atlas of Dragons")*, *[Effects of the Elder Scrolls](/wiki/Skyrim:Effects_of_the_Elder_Scrolls "Skyrim:Effects of the Elder Scrolls")*, *[Dragon Language: Myth no More](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Language:_Myth_no_More "Skyrim:Dragon Language: Myth no More")*, *[Flight from the Thalmor](/wiki/Skyrim:Flight_from_the_Thalmor "Skyrim:Flight from the Thalmor")*, and *[Remanada](/wiki/Skyrim:Remanada "Skyrim:Remanada")*.

The armory still contains the same items left previously, while in the sleeping quarters the cooking fire has been relit and now has a [cooking spit](/wiki/Skyrim:Cooking_Pot "Skyrim:Cooking Pot") hanging in front. The beds and chests are exactly as you left them; however, the small table now has a small mead barrel on top, and the longer table is now laid with two bottles of alto wine, a bottle of wine, a [baked potato](/wiki/Skyrim:Baked_Potatoes "Skyrim:Baked Potatoes"), a portion of [grilled leeks](/wiki/Skyrim:Grilled_Leeks "Skyrim:Grilled Leeks"), a salmon steak, a [seared slaughterfish](/wiki/Skyrim:Seared_Slaughterfish "Skyrim:Seared Slaughterfish") steak, a potato, several loaves of bread, and pieces of cheese. The shelving unit is also now filled with clutter.

## Notes

- All items are free to take when you arrive. This changes when you receive the quest [Paarthurnax](/wiki/Skyrim:Paarthurnax_(quest) "Skyrim:Paarthurnax (quest)"), when Esbern tells you that the Blades will not offer you their support until the quest is complete. If the quest is left uncompleted, all items in Sky Haven Temple will be considered owned, but will be free to take again after the quest is completed.
- Once a follower has become a Blade, he or she will be free to hire. This is particularly handy if your favorite followers are [hirelings](/wiki/Skyrim:Hireling "Skyrim:Hireling").
- With the [Hearthfire](/wiki/Skyrim:Hearthfire "Skyrim:Hearthfire") add-on, [Stewards](/wiki/Skyrim:Personal_Steward "Skyrim:Personal Steward") who are Blades will stay at the [house that they are steward of](/wiki/Skyrim:Construction "Skyrim:Construction"), and not go back here.
- The book *[Annals of the Dragonguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Annals_of_the_Dragonguard "Skyrim:Annals of the Dragonguard")* details the construction of Alduin's Wall in the [First Era](/wiki/Lore:First_Era#1E_2812 "Lore:First Era").
- The temple is mentioned in the book *[The Rise and Fall of the Blades](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Rise_and_Fall_of_the_Blades "Skyrim:The Rise and Fall of the Blades")*.
- Alduin's Wall was called [Reman](/wiki/Lore:Reman "Lore:Reman")'s Wall at some point in development of the game, as hinted by concept art.
- In the river west below from the high mountain courtyard, there's a boat containing gems, it's also noted in the [Reachwater Rock](/wiki/Skyrim:Reachwater_Rock "Skyrim:Reachwater Rock") page.

## Bugs

- Dialogue for Sky Haven Temple is only supposed to be used by Blade recruits when they're here. [Official Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim:Patch "Skyrim:Patch") 1.9 removed the condition, which then broke recruit responses outside of the temple if they are your current follower.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.0.0, fixes this bug.
- Not all of the followers that you recruit into the Blades will stay here. Check your follower's page before recruiting them, as some tend to run between here and their "former" home.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.1, fixes this bug.
- Delphine appears to have been unable to light all of the torch pits due to bad navmeshing in the cell making her unable to reach them all reliably.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.0.4, fixes this bug.
- Despite being part of The Reach and having large sections exposed to the sky above, Karthspire Redoubt (the part of Sky Haven Temple where the puzzle doors are) only ever uses fog weather which doesn't match the parent worldspace.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.0.4, fixes this bug.
- Sky Haven Temple has no designated horse markers assigned.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Legendary Edition Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Legendary_Edition_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Legendary Edition Patch"), version 3.0.1, fixes this bug.

# Skyrim:Skyborn Altar

## Overview

Skyborn Altar

**Skyborn Altar** is a mountaintop [dragon lair](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Lairs "Skyrim:Dragon Lairs") east-southeast of [Morthal](/wiki/Skyrim:Morthal "Skyrim:Morthal"). Its [word wall](/wiki/Skyrim:Word_Wall "Skyrim:Word Wall") teaches part of the [Frost Breath](/wiki/Skyrim:Frost_Breath "Skyrim:Frost Breath") [shout](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Shouts "Skyrim:Dragon Shouts").

## Related Quests

- **[Bounty: Dragon](/wiki/Skyrim:Bounty:_Dragon "Skyrim:Bounty: Dragon")**: Kill a [dragon](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon "Skyrim:Dragon") in its [lair](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Lairs "Skyrim:Dragon Lairs"). ([radiant](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant "Skyrim:Radiant"))
- **[Dragon Seekers](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Seekers "Skyrim:Dragon Seekers")**: Go to a [dragon lair](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Lairs "Skyrim:Dragon Lairs") with [Farkas](/wiki/Skyrim:Farkas "Skyrim:Farkas") or [Vilkas](/wiki/Skyrim:Vilkas "Skyrim:Vilkas") and kill the dragon. ([radiant](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant "Skyrim:Radiant"))

- This location is one of many potential targets for [one or more of the Radiant quests](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant#Quest_Locations "Skyrim:Radiant").

## Walkthrough

The path to Skyborn Altar is just south of [Labyrinthian](/wiki/Skyrim:Labyrinthian "Skyrim:Labyrinthian"); it can also be reached from the south by traveling between [Silent Moons Camp](/wiki/Skyrim:Silent_Moons_Camp "Skyrim:Silent Moons Camp") and [Dustman's Cairn](/wiki/Skyrim:Dustman%27s_Cairn "Skyrim:Dustman's Cairn"). The dirt path is marked by two stone bird heads flanking the base of the stone steps heading up from the south.

Before Dragon Rising

Before the [dragons' return](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Rising "Skyrim:Dragon Rising"), the word wall will be guarded by a [wispmother](/wiki/Skyrim:Wispmother "Skyrim:Wispmother") and her [wisps](/wiki/Skyrim:Wisp "Skyrim:Wisp"). In front of the wall is a sacrificial table, and on it is a [shrine of Akatosh](/wiki/Skyrim:Shrine_of_Akatosh "Skyrim:Shrine of Akatosh"), a dead [skeleton](/wiki/Skyrim:Skeleton "Skyrim:Skeleton"), two leveled [soul gems](/wiki/Skyrim:Soul_Gems "Skyrim:Soul Gems"), a leveled [potion](/wiki/Skyrim:Potions "Skyrim:Potions"), and a leveled weapon.

After the dragons' return, the word wall will be guarded by a leveled [dragon](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon "Skyrim:Dragon"), which is resting on the wall. There is a [dead adventurer](/wiki/Skyrim:Adventurer#Adventurer12 "Skyrim:Adventurer") slumped against the right-hand side of the wall.

Regardless of whether [Dragon Rising](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Rising "Skyrim:Dragon Rising") has been completed, the boss chest is behind the pillar to the left of the word wall, and there is a burial urn a few feet north of the chest, hidden in the rocks.

## Notes

- A [silver ore vein](/wiki/Skyrim:Silver_Ore_Vein "Skyrim:Silver Ore Vein") is a short distance southwest from the bottom of the steps.
- Three [orichalcum ore veins](/wiki/Skyrim:Orichalcum_Ore_Vein "Skyrim:Orichalcum Ore Vein") are 140 feet southeast of the altar [(map)](https://gamemap.uesp.net/sr/?world=Skyrim&x=-3047&y=46305&zoom=16&legacy=true).
- A [moonstone ore vein](/wiki/Skyrim:Moonstone_Ore_Vein "Skyrim:Moonstone Ore Vein") is in a gap in the rocks to the northeast, between the altar and the [Shrine of Mehrunes Dagon](/wiki/Skyrim:Shrine_of_Mehrunes_Dagon "Skyrim:Shrine of Mehrunes Dagon") [(map)](https://gamemap.uesp.net/sr/?world=Skyrim&x=-3047&y=46305&zoom=16&legacy=true).
- An adept-locked chest is due south of the word wall. Follow the path down two flights of stairs, past the first tree on the left with a lump of rock next to it, and turn due east at the second tree. The chest is behind the tree, against the rock face.
- The dragon's death animation may plow into the rock from the north and leave a trail but no dragon. Climb down to the north to find the dragon's body.

## Bugs

- This location might not be marked as cleared even after killing all inhabitants.
  - Reloading a save before clearing it and trying again will fix this.
- The map marker location data for Skyborn Altar points to a random XMarker rather than to the map marker itself.
  - The [Unofficial Skyrim Special Edition Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Special_Edition_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Special Edition Patch"), version 4.2.3, fixes this bug.

# Skyrim:Skybound Watch Pass

## Overview

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| |  | | --- | | Pass: Skybound Watch Pass ([view on map](https://gamemap.uesp.net/sr/?world=Skyrim&centeron=Skybound+Watch+Pass)) | | |

| [Clearable](/wiki/Skyrim:Dungeons#Clearing "Skyrim:Dungeons") | Yes |

| [Respawn Time](/wiki/Skyrim:Respawn "Skyrim:Respawn") | 10 days or 30 days |
| [Level](/wiki/Skyrim:Encounter_Zone_Level "Skyrim:Encounter Zone Level") | Min: 6 |
| Occupants | |
| [Bandits](/wiki/Skyrim:Bandit "Skyrim:Bandit"), [Giant Frostbite Spider](/wiki/Skyrim:Giant_Frostbite_Spider "Skyrim:Giant Frostbite Spider") | |

| *[Battle of Red Mountain](/wiki/Skyrim:Battle_of_Red_Mountain "Skyrim:Battle of Red Mountain")* | |

| SouthSkyboundWatchExterior01, SouthSkyboundWatchExterior02, SouthSkyboundWatchExterior03, SouthSkyboundWatchExterior04, NorthSkyboundWatchExterior01, NorthSkyboundWatchExterior02, NorthSkyboundWatchExterior03, SkyboundPass01 | |
| Region | |
| [Falkreath Hold](/wiki/Skyrim:Falkreath_Hold "Skyrim:Falkreath Hold") | |
| Location | |
| Northeast of [Helgen](/wiki/Skyrim:Helgen "Skyrim:Helgen") West of [Orphan Rock](/wiki/Skyrim:Orphan_Rock "Skyrim:Orphan Rock") | |

Skybound Watch Pass

**Skybound Watch Pass** is a small [Nordic tower](/wiki/Skyrim:Nordic_Towers "Skyrim:Nordic Towers") and [ruin](/wiki/Skyrim:Nordic_Dwellings "Skyrim:Nordic Dwellings") northeast of [Helgen](/wiki/Skyrim:Helgen "Skyrim:Helgen") containing [bandits](/wiki/Skyrim:Bandit "Skyrim:Bandit") and a [giant frostbite spider](/wiki/Skyrim:Giant_Frostbite_Spider "Skyrim:Giant Frostbite Spider"). It contains only one zone, *[Skybound Watch Pass](#Skybound_Watch_Pass)*.

Although the interior of the pass is named "Skybound Watch Pass", the map markers are named "South Skybound Watch" and "North Skybound Watch", counting as two separate locations for the "Locations Discovered" statistic. The southern entrance is displayed on the map as a  [Nordic tower](/wiki/Skyrim:Nordic_Towers "Skyrim:Nordic Towers") [(map)](https://gamemap.uesp.net/sr/?world=Skyrim&centeron=South+Skybound+Watch&zoom=14&legacy=true), while the northern entrance is displayed as a  [Nordic dwelling](/wiki/Skyrim:Nordic_Dwellings "Skyrim:Nordic Dwellings") [(map)](https://gamemap.uesp.net/sr/?world=Skyrim&centeron=North+Skybound+Watch&zoom=14&legacy=true). The southern entrance is south of [Riverwood](/wiki/Skyrim:Riverwood "Skyrim:Riverwood"), and the northern entrance is southeast of the town.

## Related Quests

- **[Destruction Ritual Spell](/wiki/Skyrim:Destruction_Ritual_Spell "Skyrim:Destruction Ritual Spell")**: Learn the most powerful [Destruction](/wiki/Skyrim:Destruction "Skyrim:Destruction") spells Skyrim has to offer.

### Exterior: South Skybound Watch

South Skybound Watch

The path that leads up to the pass from near [Orphan Rock](/wiki/Skyrim:Orphan_Rock "Skyrim:Orphan Rock") is guarded by a [wispmother](/wiki/Skyrim:Wispmother "Skyrim:Wispmother") and three [wisps](/wiki/Skyrim:Wisp "Skyrim:Wisp"). The tower has a novice-locked [chest](/wiki/Skyrim:Chest "Skyrim:Chest") at the very top, a random [helmet](/wiki/Skyrim:Helmet "Skyrim:Helmet") on top of a broken stone table on the level below, and a random [potion](/wiki/Skyrim:Potions "Skyrim:Potions") of [healing](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Minor_Healing "Skyrim:Potion of Minor Healing"), [magicka](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Minor_Magicka "Skyrim:Potion of Minor Magicka"), or [stamina](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Minor_Stamina "Skyrim:Potion of Minor Stamina") on a shelf to the immediate right of the iron door leading into the interior of the pass.

### Exterior: North Skybound Watch

North Skybound Watch

Three bandits reside in the remains of the guardhouse. As you enter through the arch to their sleeping area there is a partly buried [burial urn](/wiki/Skyrim:Burial_Urn "Skyrim:Burial Urn") on your left, with a random [war axe](/wiki/Skyrim:War_Axe "Skyrim:War Axe") lying on a broken sideboard. Opposite the arch you enter through is an iron door, with a [rabbit](/wiki/Skyrim:Rabbit_(dead) "Skyrim:Rabbit (dead)") hanging from a rack and a [pheasant](/wiki/Skyrim:Pheasant "Skyrim:Pheasant") on the ground beneath it. To the right of the door is a table and two chairs holding a [rabbit haunch](/wiki/Skyrim:Rabbit_Haunch "Skyrim:Rabbit Haunch") and a medium [coin purse](/wiki/Skyrim:Coin_Purse "Skyrim:Coin Purse"). Next to the table is a small cage and beside this is a random [warhammer](/wiki/Skyrim:Warhammer "Skyrim:Warhammer"), and a bench with a copy of *[Yellow Book of Riddles](/wiki/Skyrim:Yellow_Book_of_Riddles "Skyrim:Yellow Book of Riddles")* on top. An empty pot hangs above the campfire in the middle of the room, with two unowned bedrolls beside it. Through the door is a lookout point with a pedestal at the end used for the quest [Destruction Ritual Spell](/wiki/Skyrim:Destruction_Ritual_Spell "Skyrim:Destruction Ritual Spell"), while to the left is a novice-locked chest. Follow the stairs down on the right to find the door leading to the interior section of the pass.

### Skybound Watch Pass

The passage links the lowlands of [Whiterun Hold](/wiki/Skyrim:Whiterun_Hold "Skyrim:Whiterun Hold") to the mountainous portion of [Falkreath Hold](/wiki/Skyrim:Falkreath_Hold "Skyrim:Falkreath Hold") and is divided into three small sections. On either end of the passage are a number of bandits that are cut off by a giant frostbite spider's lair.

Entering from the south leads down a flight of stairs to a room containing a large amount of [hanging moss](/wiki/Skyrim:Hanging_Moss "Skyrim:Hanging Moss") and several [jazbay grapes](/wiki/Skyrim:Jazbay_Grapes "Skyrim:Jazbay Grapes"), with a stairwell in the middle. Wooden spiral stairs lead down to a passage, where three bandits wait. There is an [urn](/wiki/Skyrim:Urn "Skyrim:Urn") on your right, and a bit farther, a burial urn on your left. This portion of passage is slightly flooded and contains a large amount of hanging moss. There is an unlocked chest against the east wall, which is trapped with an apprentice-level [tension cable](/wiki/Skyrim:Tension_Cable "Skyrim:Tension Cable") that triggers [dart traps](/wiki/Skyrim:Dart_Trap "Skyrim:Dart Trap") to fire from the wall. To avoid damage, either disarm before opening, or just stand to the side until they stop. The passage leads to a door, with a giant frostbite spider on the other side of the door facing toward you.

Entering from the northern entrance you will immediately see a couple of bedrolls and then eight hanging moss growing from the ceiling. If sneaking you will see the first of two bandits sitting at the top of a flight of stairs part way down, with the other just to the right out of sight. Beyond the bandits is a [pressure plate](/wiki/Skyrim:Pressure_Plate "Skyrim:Pressure Plate") that triggers a [battering ram](/wiki/Skyrim:Battering_Ram "Skyrim:Battering Ram"). At the bottom of the stairs is a campfire in front of a set of shelves holding various [fur armor](/wiki/Skyrim:Fur_Armor "Skyrim:Fur Armor"), a pair of random [light boots](/wiki/Skyrim:Light_Boots "Skyrim:Light Boots"), two small coin purses, and a copy of the [Block](/wiki/Skyrim:Block "Skyrim:Block") [skill book](/wiki/Skyrim:Skill_Books "Skyrim:Skill Books") *[Battle of Red Mountain](/wiki/Skyrim:Battle_of_Red_Mountain "Skyrim:Battle of Red Mountain")*. On a sideboard there is a novice-locked chest and a random [potion of healing](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Minor_Healing "Skyrim:Potion of Minor Healing"), with a piece of fur armor on the floor next to it. Through the door you will see webbing and spider egg sacs, one of which is harvestable. Follow the stairs down past another harvestable egg sac and several lootable dessicated corpses and web sacs. At the bottom you will encounter the same giant frostbite spider.

## Notes

- The pass contains 23 samples of hanging moss and 8 samples of jazbay grapes.
- A [moonstone ore vein](/wiki/Skyrim:Moonstone_Ore_Vein "Skyrim:Moonstone Ore Vein") is 240 feet east-southeast of the North Skybound Watch entrance, on the east side of the valley roughly halfway to Orphan Rock.
